  "sectionOcrText": "## **9.1 How to Analyse Chemical Composition?**\n\nWe can continue asking in the same way, what type of organic compounds are found in living organisms? How does one go about finding the answer? To get an answer, one has to perform a chemical analysis.\n\nWe can take any living tissue (a vegetable or a piece of liver, etc.) and grind it in trichloroacetic acid (Cl₃CCOOH) using a mortar and pestle. We obtain a thick slurry. If we were to strain this through a cheesecloth or cotton, we would obtain two fractions. One is called the **filtrate** (or more technically, the acid-soluble pool), and the other is the **retentate** (the acid-insoluble fraction).\n\nScientists have found thousands of organic compounds in the acid-soluble pool.\n\nIn higher classes, you will learn about how to analyse a living tissue sample and identify a particular organic compound. It will involve several separation techniques. The compounds are separated from all other compounds and analysed to determine their structures.\n\nAnalytical techniques, when applied to the compound, reveal its molecular structure. Thousands of compounds that we get from living tissues can be called **biomolecules**. However, living organisms also contain inorganic elements and compounds.\n\n---\n\n### Table 9.1 Comparison of Elements Present in Living and Non-Living Matter\n\nThe table compares the percentage composition of:\n\n* Carbon\n* Hydrogen\n* Oxygen\n* Nitrogen\n* Sulphur\n* Sodium\n* Calcium\n* Magnesium\n\nin the Earth's crust and in the human body.\n\n---\n\nLiving organisms have both organic and inorganic constituents.\n\nHow do we know this?\n\nA slightly destructive experiment has to be done.\n\nOne weighs a small amount of living tissue (say 1 g), then dries it completely and records the dry weight. The tissue is then fully burnt. All the carbon compounds are oxidised to carbon dioxide, water vapour and nitrogen oxides. The remaining inorganic material is called **ash**.\n\nThis ash contains inorganic constituents such as:\n\n* Calcium\n* Magnesium\n* etc.\n\nThese are therefore found in the **acid-insoluble fraction**.\n\nChemical analysis thus gives an idea of:\n\n* organic compounds\n* inorganic compounds\n\npresent in living tissues.\n\n---\n\nAmong the organic compounds commonly found are:\n\n* Amino acids\n* Sugars\n* Lipids\n* Nucleotides\n* Nucleic acids\n* Proteins\n\n---\n\n## Amino Acids\n\nAmino acids are organic compounds containing both an amino group (–NH₂) and a carboxyl group (–COOH).\n\nThe carbon atom to which these groups are attached also carries a variable **R-group**.\n\nExamples include:\n\n* Glycine (R = H)\n* Alanine (R = CH₃)\n* Serine (R = CH₂OH)\n\nThese amino acids differ only in their side chain (R-group).\n\n---\n\n### Zwitterionic Form\n\nAt physiological pH, amino acids exist predominantly in the **zwitterionic form**, possessing both positive and negative charges.\n\n*(Figure showing glycine in zwitterionic form.)*\n\n---\n\n## Lipids\n\nLipids are generally **water insoluble**.\n\nA fatty acid has:\n\n* one carboxyl group (–COOH)\n* attached to a hydrocarbon chain.\n\nFatty acids may be:\n\n* **Saturated** (no double bonds)\n* **Unsaturated** (one or more double bonds)\n\nExamples include:\n\n* Palmitic acid\n* Arachidonic acid\n\nLipids such as **triglycerides** consist of glycerol and fatty acids.\n\nBased on melting point:\n\n* Oils remain liquid at room temperature.\n* Fats are solid.\n\nSome lipids contain phosphorus and are called **phospholipids**.\n\nPhospholipids are major components of the **cell membrane**.\n\n---\n\n## Nucleotides and Nucleic Acids\n\nLiving organisms contain nitrogenous bases such as:\n\n* Adenine\n* Guanine\n* Cytosine\n* Uracil\n* Thymine\n\nWhen attached to sugar, they form **nucleosides**.\n\nWhen phosphate is also attached, they form **nucleotides**.\n\nDNA and RNA are polymers of nucleotides and function as the **genetic material**.\n\n",

    "section_text": {
      "has_text": true,
      "normalized_text": "## **9.1 How to Analyse Chemical Composition?**\n\nWe can continue asking in the same way, what type of organic compounds are found in living organisms? How does one go about finding the answer? To get an answer, one has to perform a chemical analysis.\n\nWe can take any living tissue (a vegetable or a piece of liver, etc.) and grind it in trichloroacetic acid (Cl₃CCOOH) using a mortar and pestle. We obtain a thick slurry. If we were to strain this through a cheesecloth or cotton, we would obtain two fractions. One is called the **filtrate** (or more technically, the acid-soluble pool), and the other is the **retentate** (the acid-insoluble fraction).\n\nScientists have found thousands of organic compounds in the acid-soluble pool.\n\nIn higher classes, you will learn about how to analyse a living tissue sample and identify a particular organic compound. It will involve several separation techniques. The compounds are separated from all other compounds and analysed to determine their structures.\n\nAnalytical techniques, when applied to the compound, reveal its molecular structure. Thousands of compounds that we get from living tissues can be called **biomolecules**. However, living organisms also contain inorganic elements and compounds.\n\n---\n\n### Table 9.1 Comparison of Elements Present in Living and Non-Living Matter\n\nThe table compares the percentage composition of:\n\n* Carbon\n* Hydrogen\n* Oxygen\n* Nitrogen\n* Sulphur\n* Sodium\n* Calcium\n* Magnesium\n\nin the Earth's crust and in the human body.\n\n---\n\nLiving organisms have both organic and inorganic constituents.\n\nHow do we know this?\n\nA slightly destructive experiment has to be done.\n\nOne weighs a small amount of living tissue (say 1 g), then dries it completely and records the dry weight. The tissue is then fully burnt. All the carbon compounds are oxidised to carbon dioxide, water vapour and nitrogen oxides. The remaining inorganic material is called **ash**.\n\nThis ash contains inorganic constituents such as:\n\n* Calcium\n* Magnesium\n* etc.\n\nThese are therefore found in the **acid-insoluble fraction**.\n\nChemical analysis thus gives an idea of:\n\n* organic compounds\n* inorganic compounds\n\npresent in living tissues.\n\n---\n\nAmong the organic compounds commonly found are:\n\n* Amino acids\n* Sugars\n* Lipids\n* Nucleotides\n* Nucleic acids\n* Proteins\n\n---\n\n## Amino Acids\n\nAmino acids are organic compounds containing both an amino group (–NH₂) and a carboxyl group (–COOH).\n\nThe carbon atom to which these groups are attached also carries a variable **R-group**.\n\nExamples include:\n\n* Glycine (R = H)\n* Alanine (R = CH₃)\n* Serine (R = CH₂OH)\n\nThese amino acids differ only in their side chain (R-group).\n\n---\n\n### Zwitterionic Form\n\nAt physiological pH, amino acids exist predominantly in the **zwitterionic form**, possessing both positive and negative charges.\n\n*(Figure showing glycine in zwitterionic form.)*\n\n---\n\n## Lipids\n\nLipids are generally **water insoluble**.\n\nA fatty acid has:\n\n* one carboxyl group (–COOH)\n* attached to a hydrocarbon chain.\n\nFatty acids may be:\n\n* **Saturated** (no double bonds)\n* **Unsaturated** (one or more double bonds)\n\nExamples include:\n\n* Palmitic acid\n* Arachidonic acid\n\nLipids such as **triglycerides** consist of glycerol and fatty acids.\n\nBased on melting point:\n\n* Oils remain liquid at room temperature.\n* Fats are solid.\n\nSome lipids contain phosphorus and are called **phospholipids**.\n\nPhospholipids are major components of the **cell membrane**.\n\n---\n\n## Nucleotides and Nucleic Acids\n\nLiving organisms contain nitrogenous bases such as:\n\n* Adenine\n* Guanine\n* Cytosine\n* Uracil\n* Thymine\n\nWhen attached to sugar, they form **nucleosides**.\n\nWhen phosphate is also attached, they form **nucleotides**.\n\nDNA and RNA are polymers of nucleotides and function as the **genetic material**.",
